<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">FIFA Club World Cup</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>

<p>The <b>FIFA Club World Cup</b> is an <a href="/wiki/International" title="International">international</a> men's <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> competition organised by the <i><a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">Fédération Internationale de Football Association</a></i> (FIFA), the sport's global <a href="/wiki/Sports_governing_body" title="Sports governing body">governing body</a>. The competition was first contested in 2000 as the <b>FIFA Club World Championship</b>. It was not held between 2001 and 2004 due to a combination of factors, most importantly the collapse of FIFA's marketing partner <a href="/wiki/International_Sport_and_Leisure" title="International Sport and Leisure">International Sport and Leisure</a>. Since <a href="/wiki/2005_FIFA_Club_World_Championship" title="2005 FIFA Club World Championship">2005</a>, the competition has been held every year, and has been hosted by Brazil, Japan, the United Arab Emirates and Morocco. The FIFA Club World Cup's prestige is perceived quite differently in different parts of the football world: while it is widely regarded as the most distinguished club level trophy in most of the world, it struggles to attract interest in most of Europe.</p>
<p>The first FIFA Club World Championship took place in Brazil in <a href="/wiki/2000_FIFA_Club_World_Championship" title="2000 FIFA Club World Championship">2000</a>. It ran in parallel with the <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_Cup_(football)" title="Intercontinental Cup (football)">Intercontinental Cup</a> (also known as European/South American Cup), a competition organised jointly by the <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">Union of European Football Associations</a> (UEFA) and the <a href="/wiki/CONMEBOL" title="CONMEBOL">Confederación Sudamericana de Fútbol</a> (CONMEBOL) first disputed in 1960 by the winners of the European Champions' Cup and the Copa Libertadores. In 2005, after the Intercontinental Cup's <a href="/wiki/2004_Intercontinental_Cup" title="2004 Intercontinental Cup">last edition</a>, that competition was merged with the <a href="/wiki/2000_FIFA_Club_World_Championship" title="2000 FIFA Club World Championship">Club World Cup's pilot edition</a> and renamed the "FIFA Club World Championship". In 2006, the tournament took its current name.</p>
<p>The current format of the tournament involves seven teams competing for the title at venues within the host nation over a period of about two weeks; the winners of that year's <a href="/wiki/AFC_Champions_League" title="AFC Champions League">AFC Champions League</a> (<a href="/wiki/Asian_Football_Confederation" title="Asian Football Confederation">Asia</a>), <a href="/wiki/CAF_Champions_League" title="CAF Champions League">CAF Champions League</a> (<a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Football" title="Confederation of African Football">Africa</a>), <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF_Champions_League" title="CONCACAF Champions League">CONCACAF Champions League</a> (<a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">North America</a>), <a href="/wiki/Copa_Libertadores" title="Copa Libertadores">Copa Libertadores</a> (<a href="/wiki/CONMEBOL" title="CONMEBOL">South America</a>), <a href="/wiki/OFC_Champions_League" title="OFC Champions League">OFC Champions League</a> (<a href="/wiki/Oceania_Football_Confederation" title="Oceania Football Confederation">Oceania</a>) and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> (<a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">Europe</a>), along with the host nation's national champions, participate in a straight <a href="/wiki/Single-elimination_tournament" title="Single-elimination tournament">knock-out tournament</a>. The host nation's national champions dispute a play-off against the Oceania champions, from which the winner joins the champions of Asia, Africa and North America at the quarter-finals. The quarter-final winners go on to face the European and South American champions, who enter at the semi-final stage, for a place in the final.</p>
<p>The current champions are Spain's <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a>, who defeated Japan's <a href="/wiki/Kashima_Antlers" title="Kashima Antlers">Kashima Antlers</a> 4–2 in the <a href="/wiki/2016_FIFA_Club_World_Cup_Final" title="2016 FIFA Club World Cup Final">final</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2016_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2016 FIFA Club World Cup">2016 edition</a>, to win a second title in the competition. European teams have been the most successful, with nine titles.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_Club_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin">Origin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_Club_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sir_Thomas_Lipton_Trophy" title="Sir Thomas Lipton Trophy">Sir Thomas Lipton Trophy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copa_Rio_(international_tournament)" title="Copa Rio (international tournament)">Copa Rio (international tournament)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peque%C3%B1a_Copa_del_Mundo_de_Clubes" title="Pequeña Copa del Mundo de Clubes">Pequeña Copa del Mundo de Clubes</a></div>
<p>The first club tournament to be billed as the "<a href="/wiki/Football_World_Championship" title="Football World Championship">Football World Championship</a>" was held in <a href="/wiki/1887_World_Championship_(football)" title="1887 World Championship (football)">1887</a>, in which <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Cup" title="Scottish Cup">Scottish Cup</a> champions <a href="/wiki/Hibernian_F.C." title="Hibernian F.C.">Hibernian</a> defeated English <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> semi-finalists <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Preston_North_End" title="Preston North End">Preston North End</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> According to FIFA, the first attempt at creating a global club football tournament was in 1909, 21 years before the first FIFA World Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sir_Thomas_Lipton_Trophy" title="Sir Thomas Lipton Trophy">Sir Thomas Lipton Trophy</a> was held in Italy in 1909 and 1911, and contested by English, Italian, German and Swiss clubs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> It was won by English amateur side <a href="/wiki/West_Auckland_Town_F.C." title="West Auckland Town F.C.">West Auckland</a> on both occasions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The idea that FIFA should organise international club competitions dates from the beginning of the 1950s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> In 1951, FIFA President Jules Rimet was asked about FIFA's involvement in the <i><a href="/wiki/Copa_Rio_(international_tournament)" title="Copa Rio (international tournament)">Copa Rio</a></i>, and stated that it was not under FIFA's jurisdiction since it was organised and sponsored by the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Football_Confederation" title="Brazilian Football Confederation">Brazilian Football Confederation</a> (<i>Confederação Brasileira de Futebol</i>; CBF).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The competition was succeeded by another tournament, named <i>Torneio Octogonal Rivadavia Corrêa Meyer</i>, which was won by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Club_de_Regatas_Vasco_da_Gama" title="Club de Regatas Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_5_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_5-7">[7]</a></sup> This tournament had five Brazilian sides, and three foreign clubs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> thus, losing half of its intercontinental aspect. In December 2007, FIFA turned down Palmeiras' request to recognise the tournament as a Club World Cup since the participants were limited to two continents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_the_Maracan%C3%A3_Stadium.jpg"><img alt="An aerial view of the Maracanã Stadium in Rio de Janeiro." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Aerial_view_of_the_Maracan%C3%A3_Stadium.jpg/220px-Aerial_view_of_the_Maracan%C3%A3_Stadium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Aerial_view_of_the_Maracan%C3%A3_Stadium.jpg/330px-Aerial_view_of_the_Maracan%C3%A3_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Aerial_view_of_the_Maracan%C3%A3_Stadium.jpg/440px-Aerial_view_of_the_Maracan%C3%A3_Stadium.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_the_Maracan%C3%A3_Stadium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_do_Maracan%C3%A3" title="Estádio do Maracanã">Estádio do Maracanã</a>, the location of the first Club World Cup final in 2000 in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although the competition was discontinued, it was held in high regard. FIFA board members <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Rous" title="Stanley Rous">Stanley Rous</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ottorino_Barassi" title="Ottorino Barassi">Ottorino Barassi</a> participated personally, albeit not in their capacity as FIFA members, in the organisation of the competition in 1951.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Rous' role was attributed to the negotiations with European clubs, whereas Barassi helped form the framework of the competition. Commenting on Juventus' acceptance to participate in the tournament, the Italian press stated that "an Italian club could not be missing in such an important and worldwide-reaching event".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Because of the difficulty the CBF found in bringing European clubs to the competition, the <i><a href="/wiki/O_Estado_de_S._Paulo" title="O Estado de S. Paulo">O Estado de S. Paulo</a></i> newspaper suggested that there should be FIFA involvement in the programming of international club competitions saying that, "ideally, international tournaments, here or abroad, should be played at times set by FIFA". However, no response was received.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peque%C3%B1a_Copa_del_Mundo" title="Pequeña Copa del Mundo">Pequeña Copa del Mundo</a></i> was a tournament held in <a href="/wiki/Venezuelan_Football_Federation" title="Venezuelan Football Federation">Venezuela</a> between 1952 and 1957, with a two short revivals in 1963 and in 1965.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_6_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_6-13">[13]</a></sup> It was usually played by eight participants, half from Europe and half from South America. After the late 1950s, the tournament rapidly lost status as the pedigree of its participants decreased. This competition, along with the creation of the European Cup and the Copa Libertadores, created the groundwork of the eventual Intercontinental Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_6_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_6-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Obstacles_to_the_creation_of_the_Club_World_Cup">Obstacles to the creation of the Club World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_Club_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Obstacles to the creation of the Club World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_Cup_(football)" title="Intercontinental Cup (football)">Intercontinental Cup (football)</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interamerican_Cup" title="Interamerican Cup">Interamerican Cup</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Afro-Asian_Club_Championship" title="Afro-Asian Club Championship">Afro-Asian Club Championship</a></div>
<p>After winning the <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_Cup_(football)" title="Intercontinental Cup (football)">Intercontinental Cup</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Madrid" title="Real Madrid">Real Madrid</a> titled themselves <i>world champions</i> until FIFA stepped in and objected, citing that the competition did not include any other champions from the other confederations; FIFA stated that they can only claim to be intercontinental champions of a competition played between two organisations in which no one else had the opportunity to participate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_1_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_1-14">[14]</a></sup> FIFA failed to authorise the competition in the 1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> FIFA stated that they would prohibit the <a href="/wiki/1961_Intercontinental_Cup" title="1961 Intercontinental Cup">1961</a> edition to be played out unless the organisers regarded the competition as a friendly or a private match between two organisations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> That same year the Intercontinental Cup was first played, FIFA authorised the <a href="/wiki/1960_International_Soccer_League" title="1960 International Soccer League">International Soccer League</a> to be contested with ratification from Sir Stanley Rous, who had become the FIFA President by that point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYC_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYC-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although FIFA hoped to eventually transform the International Soccer League into a Club World Cup, the Intercontinental Cup had attracted the interest of other continents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The North and Central America confederation, CONCACAF, was created in 1961 to organise its intentions of allowing its clubs to participate in the Copa Libertadores and, by extension, the Intercontinental Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> However, their entry into both competitions was rejected. Subsequently, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CONCACAF_Champions%27_Cup" title="CONCACAF Champions' Cup">CONCACAF Champions' Cup</a> began in <a href="/wiki/1962_CONCACAF_Champions%27_Cup" title="1962 CONCACAF Champions' Cup">1962</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> FIFA was asked by CONMEBOL and UEFA in 1963 to make the Intercontinental Cup official; however, FIFA gave the same response as in 1960 and stated that they would only recognise the competition if the Asian and African champions were included.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Due to the brutality of the Argentine and Uruguayan clubs at the Intercontinental Cup, FIFA was asked several times during the late 1960s to assess penalties and regulate the tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_12_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_12-23">[23]</a></sup> However, FIFA refused each request.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The first of these requests was made in 1967, after a play-off match labelled <a href="/wiki/1967_Intercontinental_Cup" title="1967 Intercontinental Cup">The Battle of Montevideo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_14_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_14-25">[25]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Football_Association" title="Scottish Football Association">Scottish Football Association</a>, via President Willie Allan, wanted FIFA to recognise the competition in order to enforce football regulation; FIFA responded that it could not regulate a competition it did not organise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_38_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_38-26">[26]</a></sup> Allan's crusade also suffered after CONMEBOL, with the backing of its President Teofilo Salinas and the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Football_Association" title="Argentine Football Association">Argentine Football Association</a> (<i>Asociación del Fútbol Argentino</i>; AFA), refused to allow FIFA to have any hand in the competition, stating:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_13_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_13-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<table class="cquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;"><i>The CSF is the entity in charge of controlling, in South America, the organisation of the tournament between the champions of Europe and [South] America, a competition FIFA considers a friendly. We do not think it's appropriate that FIFA has to meddle in the matter.</i></td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>René Courte, FIFA's General Sub-Secretary, wrote an article shortly afterwards stating that FIFA viewed the competition as a "European-South American friendly match".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> This was confirmed by Sir Stanley Rous, who then stated that FIFA saw the Intercontinental Cup as a friendly match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> However, with the Asian and North American club competitions in place, FIFA opened the idea of supervising the competition if it included those confederations, which was met with a negative response from its participating confederations, UEFA and CONMEBOL. According to <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Rous" title="Stanley Rous">Stanley Rous</a>, <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">CONCACAF</a> and the Asian Football Confederation had requested their participation in the Intercontinental Cup, which was rejected by UEFA and CONMEBOL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Madrid newspaper <i>ABC</i> then pointed out that, though the Intercontinental Cup was not officially endorsed by FIFA, it was endorsed by UEFA and CONMEBOL, therefore being an "intercontinental jurisdiction" cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/1968_Intercontinental_Cup" title="1968 Intercontinental Cup">1968</a> and <a href="/wiki/1969_Intercontinental_Cup" title="1969 Intercontinental Cup">1969 Intercontinental Cups</a> finished in similar fashion, with <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Matt_Busby" title="Matt Busby">Matt Busby</a> insisting that "the Argentineans should be banned from all competitive football. FIFA should really step in".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Soon after, <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Rous" title="Stanley Rous">Stanley Rous</a> wrote an article for the FIFA magazine, reaffirming his desire that FIFA could create a Club World Cup featuring champion clubs of all confederations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1970, during its Congress in Mexico, FIFA officially proposed for the first time the creation of a FIFA Club World Cup, to feature champion clubs of all confederations. The proposal received a negative response from the Europeans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> In 1973, French newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/L%27%C3%89quipe" title="L'Équipe">L'Équipe</a></i>, who helped bring about the birth of the European Cup,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_7_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_7-42">[42]</a></sup> volunteered to sponsor a Club World Cup contested by the champions of Europe, South America, North America and Africa, the only continental club tournaments in existence at the time; the competition was to potentially take place in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> between September and October 1974, with an eventual final to be held at the <a href="/wiki/Parc_des_Princes" title="Parc des Princes">Parc des Princes</a>. The extreme negativity of the Europeans prevented this from happening.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_16_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_16-43">[43]</a></sup> <i>L'Équipe</i> tried once again in 1975 to create a Club World Cup, in which participants would have been the four semi-finalists of the European Cup, both finalists of the Copa Libertadores, as well as the African and Asian champions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_17_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_17-44">[44]</a></sup> However, UEFA, via its president, <a href="/wiki/Artemio_Franchi" title="Artemio Franchi">Artemio Franchi</a>, declined once again and the proposal failed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_18_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_18-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the Intercontinental Cup in danger of being dissolved,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> West Nally, a British <a href="/wiki/Marketing" title="Marketing">marketing</a> company, was hired by UEFA and CONMEBOL to find a viable solution in 1980;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota Motor Corporation</a>, via West Nally, took the competition under its wing and rebranded it as the <i>Toyota Cup</i>, a one-off match played in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Toyota invested over US$700,000 in the <a href="/wiki/1980_Intercontinental_Cup" title="1980 Intercontinental Cup">1980 edition</a> to take place in <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Olympic_Stadium_(Tokyo)" title="National Olympic Stadium (Tokyo)">National Olympic Stadium</a>, with over US$200,000 awarded to each participant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_40_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_40-52">[52]</a></sup> The Toyota Cup, with its new format, was received with scepticism, as the sport was unfamiliar in the <a href="/wiki/Far_East" title="Far East">Far East</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> However, the financial incentive was welcomed, as European and South American clubs were suffering financial difficulties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_39_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_39-55">[55]</a></sup> To protect themselves against the possibility of European withdrawals, Toyota, UEFA and every European Cup participant signed annual contracts requiring the eventual winners of the European Cup to participate at the Intercontinental Cup, as a condition UEFA stipulated to the clubs' participation in the European Cup, or risk facing an international lawsuit from UEFA and Toyota.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> In 1983, <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">The Football Association</a> tried organising a Club World Cup to be played in 1985 and sponsored by West Nally, only to be denied by UEFA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interamerican_Cup" title="Interamerican Cup">Interamerican Cup</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Afro-Asian_Club_Championship" title="Afro-Asian Club Championship">Afro-Asian Club Championship</a> were tournaments created to allow those regions their own Club competitions, in large part due to the refusal of UEFA and CONMEBOL to allow CONCACAF, AFC and CAF clubs to compete in the Intercontinental Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> According to Brazilian newspaper <i>O Estado de São Paulo</i>, the deal for the establishment of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interamerican_Cup" title="Interamerican Cup">Interamerican Cup</a> was made in 1968 by <a href="/wiki/CONMEBOL" title="CONMEBOL">CONMEBOL</a> and <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">CONCACAF</a>, and established that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interamerican_Cup" title="Interamerican Cup">Interamerican Cup</a> champion club would be entitled to represent the American continent in the Intercontinental Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> According to the Mexican newspapers, after winning the 1977 and 1980 editions of the Interamerican Cup, Mexican teams <a href="/wiki/Club_Am%C3%A9rica" title="Club América">Club América</a> and <a href="/wiki/Club_Universidad_Nacional" title="Club Universidad Nacional">Club Universidad Nacional</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Football_Federation" title="Mexican Football Federation">Mexican Football Federation</a>, demanded, unsuccessfully, to participate in the Intercontinental Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_of_the_FIFA_Club_World_Cup">Birth of the FIFA Club World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_Club_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Birth of the FIFA Club World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:INTER-CAMPE%C3%83O-MUNDIAL.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1632" data-file-width="2464" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/INTER-CAMPE%C3%83O-MUNDIAL.jpg/220px-INTER-CAMPE%C3%83O-MUNDIAL.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/INTER-CAMPE%C3%83O-MUNDIAL.jpg/330px-INTER-CAMPE%C3%83O-MUNDIAL.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/INTER-CAMPE%C3%83O-MUNDIAL.jpg/440px-INTER-CAMPE%C3%83O-MUNDIAL.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:INTER-CAMPE%C3%83O-MUNDIAL.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Sport_Club_Internacional" title="Sport Club Internacional">Sport Club Internacional</a> won the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA Club World Cup">2006 FIFA Club World Cup</a> defeating <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> 1–0 <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_Club_World_Cup_Final" title="2006 FIFA Club World Cup Final">the final</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The framework of the <a href="/wiki/2000_FIFA_Club_World_Championship" title="2000 FIFA Club World Championship">2000 FIFA Club World Championship</a> was laid years in advance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Sepp_Blatter" title="Sepp Blatter">Sepp Blatter</a>, the idea of the tournament was presented to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIFA_Executive_Committee" title="FIFA Executive Committee">Executive Committee</a> in December 1993 in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>, USA, by <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">A.C. Milan</a> president <a href="/wiki/Silvio_Berlusconi" title="Silvio Berlusconi">Silvio Berlusconi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_35_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_35-64">[64]</a></sup> Initially, there were nine candidates to host the competition, of which only Saudi Arabia, Mexico, Brazil and Uruguay confirmed their interest to FIFA. On 3 September 1997, FIFA selected Brazil to host the competition, which was initially scheduled to take place in 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The competition gave away US$28 million in prize money and its TV rights, worth US$40 million, were sold to 15 broadcasters across five continents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_28_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_28-66">[66]</a></sup> The final draw of the first Club World Championship was done on 19 October 1999 at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copacabana_Palace_Hotel" title="Copacabana Palace Hotel">Copacabana Palace Hotel</a> in Rio de Janeiro.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>The inaugural competition was planned to be contested in 1999 by the continental club winners of 1998, the Intercontinental Cup winners and the host nation's national club champions, but it was postponed by one year. When it was rescheduled, the competition had eight new participants from the continental champions of 1999: Brazilian clubs <a href="/wiki/Sport_Club_Corinthians_Paulista" title="Sport Club Corinthians Paulista">Corinthians</a> and <a href="/wiki/CR_Vasco_da_Gama" title="CR Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a>, English side Manchester United, Mexican club <a href="/wiki/Club_Necaxa" title="Club Necaxa">Necaxa</a>, Moroccan club <a href="/wiki/Raja_Casablanca" title="Raja Casablanca">Raja Casablanca</a>, Spanish side Real Madrid, Saudi club <a href="/wiki/Al-Nassr_FC" title="Al-Nassr FC">Al-Nassr</a>, and Australian club <a href="/wiki/South_Melbourne_FC" title="South Melbourne FC">South Melbourne</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The first goal of the competition was scored by Real Madrid's <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Anelka" title="Nicolas Anelka">Nicolas Anelka</a> in a 3–1 win over Al-Nassr on 5 January 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The final was an all-Brazilian affair, as well as the only one which saw one side have home advantage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_34_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_34-70">[70]</a></sup> Vasco da Gama could not take advantage of its local support, being beaten by Corinthians 4–3 on <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalties</a> after a 0–0 draw in <a href="/wiki/Overtime_(sports)#Association_football" title="Overtime (sports)">extra time</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2001_FIFA_Club_World_Championship" title="2001 FIFA Club World Championship">second edition</a> of the competition was planned for Spain in 2001, and was supposed to feature 12 clubs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_31_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_31-72">[72]</a></sup> The draw was performed at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Coru%C3%B1a" title="La Coruña">La Coruña</a> on 6 March 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> However, it was cancelled on 18 May, due to a combination of factors, most importantly the collapse of FIFA's marketing partner <a href="/wiki/International_Sport_and_Leisure" title="International Sport and Leisure">International Sport and Leisure</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The participants of the cancelled edition received US$750,000 each in compensation; the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Spanish_Football_Federation" title="Royal Spanish Football Federation">Royal Spanish Football Federation</a> (RFEF) also received US$1 million from FIFA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Another attempt to stage the competition in 2003, in which 17 countries were looking to be the host nation, also failed to happen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> FIFA agreed with UEFA, CONMEBOL and Toyota to merge the Intercontinental Cup and Club World Championship into one event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The final Intercontinental Cup was in 2004, with a relaunched Club World Championship held in Japan in December 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_33_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_33-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FC_Barcelona_Team_2011.jpg"><img alt="A group of association football players, who played for FC Barcelona at the time of the photo, lifting their coach after winning their second FIFA Club World Cup." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2288" data-file-width="3687" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/FC_Barcelona_Team_2011.jpg/220px-FC_Barcelona_Team_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/FC_Barcelona_Team_2011.jpg/330px-FC_Barcelona_Team_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/FC_Barcelona_Team_2011.jpg/440px-FC_Barcelona_Team_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FC_Barcelona_Team_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Pep_Guardiola" title="Pep Guardiola">Pep Guardiola</a> is hoisted in the air after his team won the <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2011 FIFA Club World Cup">2011 FIFA Club World Cup</a>, defeating <a href="/wiki/Santos_FC" title="Santos FC">Santos</a> 4–0 in <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_Club_World_Cup_Final" title="2011 FIFA Club World Cup Final">the final</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2005_FIFA_Club_World_Championship" title="2005 FIFA Club World Championship">2005 tournament</a> was shorter than the previous World Championship, reducing the problem of scheduling the tournament around the different club seasons across each continent. It contained just the six reigning continental champions, with the CONMEBOL and UEFA representatives receiving <a href="/wiki/Bye_(sports)" title="Bye (sports)">byes</a> to the semi-finals. A new trophy was introduced. The draw for the 2005 edition of the competition took place on 30 July 2005 at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westin_Hotels" title="Westin Hotels">The Westin Tokyo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_36_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_36-80">[80]</a></sup> In the final, one goal from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carlos_Luciano_da_Silva" title="Carlos Luciano da Silva">Mineiro</a> was enough for <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC" title="São Paulo FC">São Paulo</a> to defeat English club <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-S.C3.A3o_Paulo_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-S.C3.A3o_Paulo-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sport_Club_Internacional" title="Sport Club Internacional">Internacional</a> defeated defending world and South American champions São Paulo in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Copa_Libertadores_Finals" title="2006 Copa Libertadores Finals">2006 Copa Libertadores finals</a> in order to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA Club World Cup">2006 tournament</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> which they won with a late goal from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carlos_Adriano_de_Souza_Vieira" title="Carlos Adriano de Souza Vieira">Adriano Gabiru</a> to defeat <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_Club_World_Cup_Final" title="2006 FIFA Club World Cup Final">final</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> It was in <a href="/wiki/2007_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2007 FIFA Club World Cup">2007</a> when Brazilian hegemony was finally broken, when Milan defeated <a href="/wiki/Boca_Juniors" title="Boca Juniors">Boca Juniors</a> 4–2 in a <a href="/wiki/2007_FIFA_Club_World_Cup_Final" title="2007 FIFA Club World Cup Final">final</a> that saw players on both sides <a href="/wiki/Ejection_(sports)" title="Ejection (sports)">sent off</a>: Milan's <a href="/wiki/Kakha_Kaladze" title="Kakha Kaladze">Kakha Kaladze</a> in the 77th minute, and 11 minutes later, Boca Juniors' <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Ledesma" title="Pablo Ledesma">Pablo Ledesma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_37_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_37-85">[85]</a></sup> The following year, Manchester United saw off Ecuadorian club <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LDU_Quito" title="LDU Quito">LDU Quito</a> 1–0 to become <a href="/wiki/2008_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2008 FIFA Club World Cup">world champions</a> in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Corinthians_Club_World_Cup_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4016" data-file-width="6016" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Corinthians_Club_World_Cup_2012.jpg/220px-Corinthians_Club_World_Cup_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Corinthians_Club_World_Cup_2012.jpg/330px-Corinthians_Club_World_Cup_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Corinthians_Club_World_Cup_2012.jpg/440px-Corinthians_Club_World_Cup_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Corinthians_Club_World_Cup_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Corinthians won their second world title after defeating Chelsea 1–0 in the final.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The United Arab Emirates applied, with success, for the right to host the FIFA Club World Cup in 2009 and 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Barcelona dethroned world and European champions Manchester United in the <a href="/wiki/2009_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2009 UEFA Champions League Final">2009 UEFA Champions League final</a> to qualify for <a href="/wiki/2009_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2009 FIFA Club World Cup">that year's Club World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> After a close <a href="/wiki/2009_FIFA_Club_World_Cup_Final" title="2009 FIFA Club World Cup Final">final</a> encounter, which saw the need for extra-time, <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">Lionel Messi</a> scored from a header to snatch victory for Barcelona and complete an unprecedented <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Sextuple" title="The Sextuple">sextuple</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barcelona_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barcelona-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA Club World Cup">2010 tournament</a> saw the first team from outside Europe or South America side to reach the final: DR Congo's <a href="/wiki/TP_Mazembe" title="TP Mazembe">TP Mazembe</a> defeated Brazil's Internacional 2–0 in the semi-final to face Internazionale, who had beaten South Korean club <a href="/wiki/Seongnam_FC" title="Seongnam FC">Seongnam Ilhwa Chunma</a> 3–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Internazionale would go on to beat Mazembe with the same scoreline to complete their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tuples_in_association_football#The_Quintuple" title="Tuples in association football">quintuple</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>The FIFA Club World Cup returned to Japan for the 2011 and 2012 edition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2011 FIFA Club World Cup">2011</a>, Barcelona comfortably won their semi-final match 4–0 against Qatari club <a href="/wiki/Al_Sadd_SC" title="Al Sadd SC">Al Sadd</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> In the final, Barcelona would repeat their performance against Santos; this is, to date, the largest winning margin in the final of the competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Messi also became the first player to score in two different Club World Cup finals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lionel_Messi_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lionel_Messi-101">[101]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2012_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2012 FIFA Club World Cup">2012 edition</a> saw Europe's dominance come to an end as Corinthians, boasting over 30,000 travelling fans which was dubbed the <i>"Invasão da Fiel"</i>, travelled to Japan to join Barcelona in being two-time winners of the competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> In the semi-finals, Al-Ahly managed to keep the scoreline close as Corinthians' <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Guerrero" title="Paolo Guerrero">Paolo Guerrero</a> scored to send the <i>Timão</i> into their second final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Guerrero would once again come through for Corinthians as the <i>Timão</i> saw off English side <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> 1–0 in order to bring the trophy back to Brazil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corinthians_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Corinthians-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/2013_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2013 FIFA Club World Cup">2013</a> and <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA Club World Cup">2014</a> had the Club World Cup moving to <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>. The first edition saw a <a href="/wiki/Cinderella_(sports)" title="Cinderella (sports)">Cinderella</a> run of host team Raja Casablanca, who had to start in the play-off round and became the second African team to reach the final, after defeating Brazil's <a href="/wiki/Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro" title="Clube Atlético Mineiro">Atlético Mineiro</a> in the semi-final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Like Mazembe, Raja also lost to the European champion, this time a 2–0 defeat to <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> 2014 again had a decision between South America and Europe, and Real Madrid beat <a href="/wiki/San_Lorenzo_de_Almagro" title="San Lorenzo de Almagro">San Lorenzo</a> 2–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Performances">Performances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_Club_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Performances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_FIFA_Club_World_Cup_finals" title="List of FIFA Club World Cup finals">List of FIFA Club World Cup finals</a></div>
<p>Barcelona hold the record for most victories, winning the competition three times. Corinthians' inaugural victory remains the best result from a host nation's national league champions. Teams from Spain have won the tournament five times, the most for any nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overview_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Overview-110">[110]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Results_by_Confederation">Results by Confederation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_Club_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Results by Confederation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Africa's best representatives are TP Mazembe from the Democratic Republic of the Congo and Moroccan club Raja Casablanca. They remain the only clubs from outside Europe and South America to play in the final.</p>
<p>Mexican clubs Necaxa and <a href="/wiki/C.F._Monterrey" title="C.F. Monterrey">Monterrey</a>, as well as Costa Rica's <a href="/wiki/Deportivo_Saprissa" title="Deportivo Saprissa">Saprissa</a>, have each earned third place, North America's best results. The bronze medals by Japanese clubs <a href="/wiki/Urawa_Red_Diamonds" title="Urawa Red Diamonds">Urawa Red Diamonds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gamba_Osaka" title="Gamba Osaka">Gamba Osaka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanfrecce_Hiroshima" title="Sanfrecce Hiroshima">Sanfrecce Hiroshima</a>, South Korean club <a href="/wiki/Pohang_Steelers" title="Pohang Steelers">Pohang Steelers</a> and Qatari side Al Sadd remain as Asia's best results in the tournament. <a href="/wiki/Auckland_City_FC" title="Auckland City FC">Auckland City</a> has earned third place and is the only OFC team to reach the semi-finals.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Results_by_league">Results by league</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_Club_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Results by league">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Format_and_rules">Format and rules</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_Club_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Format and rules">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_FIFA_Club_World_Cup_participants" title="List of FIFA Club World Cup participants">List of FIFA Club World Cup participants</a></div>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center; margin-left:1em; float:right">
<caption>Distribution of clubs in the<br/>
FIFA Club World Cup<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Formats_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-Formats-154">[145]</a></sup></caption>
<tr>
<th scope="col">Play-off round</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
<div>
<ul>
<li>Winners of the <a href="/wiki/OFC_Champions_League" title="OFC Champions League">OFC Champions League</a></li>
<li>Host nation's national league champions</li>
</ul>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
<tr>

<li>Winners of the <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF_Champions_League" title="CONCACAF Champions League">CONCACAF Champions League</a></li>
<li>Winners of the <a href="/wiki/CAF_Champions_League" title="CAF Champions League">CAF Champions League</a></li>

<p>As of 2012, most teams qualify to the FIFA Club World by winning their continental competitions, be it the Asian AFC Champions League, African CAF Champions League, North American CONCACAF Champions League, South American Copa Libertadores, Oceanian OFC Champions League or European UEFA Champions League. Aside from these, the host nation's national league champions qualify as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Formats_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-Formats-154">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>The maiden edition of this competition was separated into two rounds. The eight participants were split into two groups of four teams. The winner of each group met in the final while the runners-up played for third place. The competition changed its format during the 2005 relaunch into a <a href="/wiki/Single-elimination_tournament" title="Single-elimination tournament">single-elimination tournament</a> in which teams play each other in one-off matches, with <a href="/wiki/Overtime_(sports)#Association_football" title="Overtime (sports)">extra time</a> and <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shoot-outs</a> used to decide the winner if necessary. It featured six clubs competing over a two-week period.There were three stages: the quarter-final round, the semi-final round and the final. The quarter-final stage pitted the Oceanian Champions League winners, the African Champions League winners, the Asian Champions League winners and the North American Champions League winners against each other. Afterwards, the winners of those games would go on to the semi-finals to play the European Champions League winners and South America's Copa Libertadores winners. The victors of each semi-final would play go on to play in the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Formats_154-2"><a href="#cite_note-Formats-154">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the introduction of the current format, which now has a fifth place match and a place for the host nation's national league champions, the format slightly changed. There are now four stages: the play-off round, the quarter-final round, the semi-final round and the final. The first stage pits the host nation's national league champions against the Oceanian Champions League winners. The winner of that stage would go on the quarter-finals to join the African Champions League winners, the AFC Champions League winners and the CONCACAF Champions League winners. The winners of those games would go on to the semi-finals to play the UEFA Champions League winners and South America's Copa Libertadores winners. The winners of each semi-final play each other in the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Formats_154-3"><a href="#cite_note-Formats-154">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Trophy">Trophy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_Club_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Trophy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:31%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div style="margin:0px 2em;">
<p>Just as the [FIFA] women's [World Cup] trophy had a distinct feminine note to it, so this new trophy is more masculine. It is also inspired by a classic sense of geometry and architecture, enduring concepts just like the status of a World Champion.</p>
</div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">“</div>
<div style="position: absolute; right: 0px; bottom: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">”</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">William Sawaya, designer of the <i>FIFA Club World Championship</i> trophy, commenting on the laurel; <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">Fédération Internationale de Football Association</a>, 3 January 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trophy_3_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-Trophy_3-155">[146]</a></sup></cite></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FIFA_Club_World_Cup_trophies.jpg"><img alt="The two trophies of the FIFA Club World Cup are seen." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="681" data-file-width="907" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/FIFA_Club_World_Cup_trophies.jpg/220px-FIFA_Club_World_Cup_trophies.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/FIFA_Club_World_Cup_trophies.jpg/330px-FIFA_Club_World_Cup_trophies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/FIFA_Club_World_Cup_trophies.jpg/440px-FIFA_Club_World_Cup_trophies.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FIFA_Club_World_Cup_trophies.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The original FIFA Club World Championship trophy (left) and the current FIFA Club World Cup in the Museum of SC Corinthians.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The trophy used during the inaugural competition was called the <i>FIFA Club World Championship</i> Cup. The original laurel was created by Sawaya &amp; Moroni, an Italian designer company that produces contemporary designs with cultural backgrounds and design concepts. The designing firm is based in <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>. The fully silver-coloured trophy had a weight of 4 kg (8.8 lb) and a height of 37.5 cm (14.8 in). Its base and widest points are 10 cm (3.9 in) long. The trophy had a base of two pedestals which had four rectangular pillars. Two of the four pillars had inscriptions on them; one contained the phrase, "FIFA Club World Championship" imprinted across. The other had the letters "FIFA" inscribed on it. On top, a football based on the <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998 FIFA World Cup</a> ball, the <a href="/wiki/Adidas_Tricolore" title="Adidas Tricolore">Adidas Tricolore</a>, can be seen. The production costs of the laurel was US$25,000. It was presented for the first time at <a href="/wiki/Sheraton_Hotels_and_Resorts" title="Sheraton Hotels and Resorts">Sheraton Hotels and Resorts</a> in Rio de Janeiro on 4 January 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trophy_3_155-1"><a href="#cite_note-Trophy_3-155">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trophy_2_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-Trophy_2-156">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sawaya_.26_Moroni_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sawaya_.26_Moroni-157">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Original_Trophy_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-Original_Trophy-158">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tournament, in its present format, shares its name with the current trophy, also called the <i>FIFA Club World Cup</i> or simply <i>la Copa</i>, which is awarded to the FIFA Club World Cup winner. It was unveiled at <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> on 30 July 2005 during the draw of that year's edition of the competition. The laurel was designed in 2005 in <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, United Kingdom, at <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Thomas_Fattorini_Ltd&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Thomas Fattorini Ltd (page does not exist)">Thomas Fattorini Ltd</a>, by English designer Jane Powell, alongside her assistant Dawn Forbes, at the behest of FIFA. The gold-and-silver-coloured trophy, weighing 5.2 kg (11 lb), has a height of 50 cm (20 in). Its base and widest points are also measured at exactly 20 cm (7.9 in). It is made out of a combination of <a href="/wiki/Brass" title="Brass">brass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sterling_silver" title="Sterling silver">sterling silver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gilding_metal" title="Gilding metal">gilding metal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aluminium" title="Aluminium">aluminium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chromium" title="Chromium">chrome</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rhodium" title="Rhodium">rhodium</a>. The trophy itself is gold plated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_36_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_36-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trophy_2_156-1"><a href="#cite_note-Trophy_2-156">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>The design, according to FIFA, shows six staggered pillars, representing the six participating teams from the respective six confederations, and one separate metal structure referencing the winner of the competition. They hold up a globe in the shape of a football – a consistent feature amongst almost all of FIFA's event trophies. The graceful curves and inherent strength of the trophy evoke the balletic and athletic qualities necessary to successfully compete in the FIFA Club World Cup and the tension and movement describe the competitive energy amongst the participants. The golden pedestal has the phrase, "FIFA Club World Cup", imprinted at the bottom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trophy_2_156-2"><a href="#cite_note-Trophy_2-156">[147]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_Club_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup_awards" title="FIFA Club World Cup awards">FIFA Club World Cup awards</a></div>
<p>At the end of each Club World Cup, awards are presented to the players and teams for accomplishments other than their final team positions in the tournament. There are currently four awards:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Award_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-Award-159">[150]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rooney_CL.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1303" data-file-width="959" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Rooney_CL.jpg/170px-Rooney_CL.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Rooney_CL.jpg/255px-Rooney_CL.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Rooney_CL.jpg/340px-Rooney_CL.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rooney_CL.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchester_United" title="Manchester United">Manchester United</a> displayed the FIFA Club World Cup Champions Badge on their jerseys</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup_awards#Golden_Ball" title="FIFA Club World Cup awards">Golden Ball</a> for the best player, determined by a vote of media members; the Silver Ball and the Bronze Ball are awarded to the players finishing second and third in the voting respectively;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Award_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-Award-159">[150]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup_awards#Golden_Boot" title="FIFA Club World Cup awards">Golden Boot</a> (sometimes called the <i>Golden Shoe</i>) for the top goalscorer; the Silver Boot and the Bronze Boot have been awarded to the second and third top goalscorers respectively;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Award_159-2"><a href="#cite_note-Award-159">[150]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup_awards#FIFA_Fair_Play_Trophy" title="FIFA Club World Cup awards">FIFA Fair Play Trophy</a> for the team with the best record of <a href="/wiki/Sportsmanship" title="Sportsmanship">fair play</a>, according to the points system and criteria established by the FIFA Fair Play Committee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Award_159-3"><a href="#cite_note-Award-159">[150]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup_awards#Most_Valuable_Player_of_the_Final_Match_Trophy" title="FIFA Club World Cup awards">Most Valuable Player of the Final Match Trophy</a> for the best performing player in the FIFA Club World Cup final. It was first awarded in 2005. The MVP of the Final Match is also rewarded with an automobile by Toyota, the presenting sponsor of the FIFA Club World Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Award_159-4"><a href="#cite_note-Award-159">[150]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The winners of the competition also receive the <i>FIFA Club World Cup Champions Badge</i>; it features an image of the trophy, which the reigning champion is entitled to display on its kit until the final of the next championship. The first edition of the badge was presented to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AC_Milan" title="AC Milan">AC Milan</a>, the winners of the <a href="/wiki/2007_FIFA_Club_World_Cup_Final" title="2007 FIFA Club World Cup Final">2007 final</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[151]</a></sup> All four previous champions were allowed to wear the badge until the <a href="/wiki/2008_FIFA_Club_World_Cup_Final" title="2008 FIFA Club World Cup Final">2008 final</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> gained the sole right to wear the badge by winning the trophy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Badge_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-Badge-161">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>Each tournament's top three teams receives a set of gold, silver or bronze medals to distribute to their players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Award_159-5"><a href="#cite_note-Award-159">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prize_money">Prize money</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_Club_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Prize money">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center; margin-left:1em; float:right">
<caption>Prize money</caption>
<tr>
<td align="center" bgcolor="gold">Winner</td>
<td>US$5 million</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center" bgcolor="silver">Runner-up</td>
<td>US$4 million</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center" bgcolor="#CC9966">Third place</td>
<td>US$2.5 million</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">Fourth place</td>
<td>US$2 million</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">Fifth place</td>
<td>US$1.5 million</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">Sixth place</td>
<td>US$1 million</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="center">Seventh place</td>
<td>US$0.5 million</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2000_FIFA_Club_World_Championship" title="2000 FIFA Club World Championship">2000 FIFA Club World Championship</a> was the inaugural edition of this competition; it provided US$28 million in prize money for its participants. The prize money received by the clubs participating was divided into fixed payments based on participation and results. Clubs finishing the tournament from fifth to eighth place received US$2.5 million. The club who would eventually finish in fourth place received US$3 million while the third-place team received US$4 million. The runner-up earned US$5 million while the eventual champions would gain US$6 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_32_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_32-162">[153]</a></sup></p>
<p>The relaunch of the tournament in <a href="/wiki/2005_FIFA_Club_World_Championship" title="2005 FIFA Club World Championship">2005 FIFA Club World Championship</a> saw different amounts of prize money given and some changes in the criteria of receiving certain amounts. The total amount of prize money given dropped to US$16 million. The winners received US$5 million and the runners-up US$4 million, with $2.5 million for third place, US$2 million for fourth, US$1.5 million for fifth and US$1 million for sixth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_29_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_29-163">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_29_163-1"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_29-163">[154]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the <a href="/wiki/2007_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2007 FIFA Club World Cup">2007 FIFA Club World Cup</a>, a play-off match between the <a href="/wiki/Oceania_Football_Confederation" title="Oceania Football Confederation">OFC</a> champions and the host-nation champions for entry into the quarter-final stage was introduced in order to increase home interest in the tournament. The reintroduction of the match for fifth place for the <a href="/wiki/2008_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2008 FIFA Club World Cup">2008 competition</a> also prompted an increase in prize money by US$500,000 to a total of US$16.5 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2008Changes_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-2008Changes-164">[155]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FIFA_Club_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Sponsorship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Like the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a>, the FIFA Club World Cup is sponsored by a group of multinational corporations. <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota Motor Corporation</a>, a Japanese <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automaker" title="Automaker">automaker</a> headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Toyota,_Aichi" title="Toyota, Aichi">Toyota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aichi_Prefecture" title="Aichi Prefecture">Aichi</a>, Japan, was the Presenting Partner of the FIFA Club World Cup until its sponsorship agreement expired at the end of December 2014 and was not renewed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[156]</a></sup> Because Toyota was an automobile manufacturer and the main sponsor of the tournament, <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Motor_Group" title="Hyundai Motor Group">Hyundai-Kia</a>'s status as a FIFA partner was not active with respect to the Club World Cup prior to 2015. However, the other FIFA partners – <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Visa_Inc." title="Visa Inc.">Visa</a> – retained full sponsorship rights. From 2015 to 2022, the tournament will be presented by <a href="/wiki/Alibaba_Group" title="Alibaba Group">Alibaba E-Auto</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>The inaugural competition had six event sponsors: <a href="/wiki/Fujifilm" title="Fujifilm">Fujifilm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hyundai" title="Hyundai">Hyundai</a>, <a href="/wiki/JVC" title="JVC">JVC</a>, <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Budweiser" title="Budweiser">Budweiser</a>, and <a href="/wiki/MasterCard" title="MasterCard">MasterCard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reference_28_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-Reference_28-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Toyota_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-Toyota-167">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Secondary_Sponsors_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-Secondary_Sponsors-168">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>Individual clubs may wear jerseys with advertising, even if such sponsors conflict with those of the FIFA Club World Cup. However, only one main sponsor is permitted per jersey in addition to that of the kit manufacturer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Formats_154-4"><a href="#cite_note-Formats-154">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tournament's current event sponsors and brands advertised (in <i>italic</i>) are:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Secondary_Sponsors_168-1"><a href="#cite_note-Secondary_Sponsors-168">[159]</a></sup></p>
